href="/wiki/Line_of_succession_to_the_British_throne" class="mw-redirect" title="Line of succession to the British throne">royal succession</a>, ending the male-preference <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">primogeniture</a> that was mandated by the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Settlement_1701" title="Act of Settlement 1701">Act of Settlement 1701</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The amendment, once enacted, will also end the ban on the monarch marrying a Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Scottish_Independence_referendum">2014 Scottish Independence referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: 2014 Scottish Independence referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">Scottish independence referendum, 2014</a></div>\n<p>On 18 September, a referendum was held in Scotland on whether to leave the United Kingdom and become an independent country. The three UK-wide political parties\xe2\x80\x94Labour, Conservative and Liberal Democrats\xe2\x80\x94campaigned together as part of the <a href="/wiki/Better_Together_(campaign)" title="Better Together (campaign)">Better Together</a> campaign while the pro-independence Scottish National Party was the main force in the <a href="/wiki/Yes_Scotland" title="Yes Scotland">Yes Scotland</a> campaign, together with the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Socialist_Party" title="Scottish Socialist Party">Scottish Socialist Party</a>. Days before the vote, with the opinion polls closing, the three Better Together party leaders issued <a href="/wiki/The_Vow_(devolution_promise)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Vow (devolution promise)">\'The Vow\'</a>, a promise of more powers for Scotland in the event of a No vote. The referendum resulted in Scotland voting by 55% to 45% to remain part of the United Kingdom.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_election">2015 election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: 2015 election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 election</a> was held on 7 May 2015 with pre-election polls all predicting a close race and a hung parliament. The surprising result on the night was a clear victory by the Conservative Party: with 37% of the popular vote, they won a narrow overall majority in parliament with 331 of the 650 seats.\n</p><p>The other most significant result of the election was the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> winning all but three of the 59 seats in Scotland, a gain of 50. This had been widely forecast as opinion polls had recorded a surge in support for the SNP following the 2014 independence referendum, and SNP party membership had more than quadrupled from 25,000 to over 100,000, meaning that 1 in every 50 of the population of Scotland was a party member.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Labour suffered its worst defeat since 1987, taking only 31% of the votes and losing 40 of its 41 seats in Scotland. The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> lost 49 of their 57 seats, as they were punished for their decision to form a coalition with the conservatives in 2010. The <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a> (UKIP), rallying voters against the European Union and against uncontrolled immigration, secured 13% of the vote and came second in over 115 races, but won only one seat in parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Cameron had a mandate for his austerity policies to shrink the size of government, and a challenge in dealing with Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> Likewise the Green Party of England and Wales saw a rise in support but retained just its one MP.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_EU_referendum">2016 EU referendum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: 2016 EU referendum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a></div>\n<p>On 20 February 2016, British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> announced that a referendum on the UK\'s membership of the European Union would be held on 23 June 2016, following years of campaigning by <a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">eurosceptics</a>. Debates and campaigns by parties supporting both "Remain" and "Leave" focused on concerns regarding <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">single market</a>, <a href="/wiki/Security" title="Security">security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a>. The result of the referendum was in favour of the country leaving the EU with 51.9% of voters wanting to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTEUBrexit_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEUBrexit-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> After the result was declared, Cameron announced that he would resign by October.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> In the event, he stood down on 13 July, with <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> becoming Prime Minister.\n</p><p>The UK remains a member of the EU for the time being, but invoked Article 50 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> on 29 March 2017.  This started negotiations on a withdrawal agreement that will last no more than two years (unless the Council and the UK agree to extend the negotiation period), before an <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">exit from the European Union</a> on 29 March 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCEUBrexit_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCEUBrexit-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The longer-term implications of the referendum vote remain uncertain, with politicians and commentators suggesting various outcomes.<sup id="cite_ref-SturgeonBBC20160626_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SturgeonBBC20160626-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bracksies_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bracksies-262">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historiography">Historiography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Historiography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Historiography of the United Kingdom">Historiography of the United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_the_British_Empire" title="Historiography of the British Empire">Historiography of the British Empire</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; Wales</a></li></ul></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The terms <i>One Kingdom</i>, <i>United Kingdom</i> and <i>United Kingdom of Great Britain</i> were used in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Union" title="Treaty of Union">Treaty of Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1707" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Union 1707">Act of Union 1707</a>. However, the actual name of the new state was <i>Great Britain</i>. The name <i>Great Britain</i> (then sometimes spelled <i>Great Brittaine</i>) was first used by James VI/I in October 1603, who indicated that henceforth he and his successors would be viewed as Kings of Great Britain, not Kings of England and Scotland. However the name was not applied to the <i>state</i> as a unit; both England and Scotland continued to be governed independently. Its validity as a name of the Crown is also questioned, given that monarchs continued using separate ordinals (e.g., James VI/I, James VII/II) in England and Scotland. To avoid confusion, historians generally avoid using the term <i>King of Great Britain</i> until 1707 and instead to match the ordinal usage call the monarchs kings or queens of England and Scotland. Separate ordinals were abandoned when the two states merged in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">1707 Acts of Union</a>, with subsequent monarchs using ordinals apparently based on English not Scottish history (it might be argued that the monarchs have simply taken the higher ordinal, which to date has always been English). One example is Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom</a>, who is referred to as being "the Second" even though there never was an Elizabeth I of Scotland or Great Britain. Thus the term <i>Great Britain</i> is generally used from 1707.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-wales-politics-23919439">New Act of Union would strengthen UK, says Fabricant</a> BBC News, accessed 1 September 2013</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation episode"><a href="/wiki/Simon_Schama" title="Simon Schama">Simon Schama</a> (presenter) (22 May 2001). R. <i>Modern Historians on British History 1485\xe2\x80\x931945: A Critical Bibliography 1945\xe2\x80\x931969</i> (1969), annotated guide to 1000 history books on every major topic, plus book reviews and major scholarly articles. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/in.ernet.dli.2015.176158">online</a></li>\n<li>Furber, Elizabeth Chapin, ed. <i>Changing Views on British History</i> (1966)</li>\n<li>Jones, Harriet, and Mark Clapson, eds. <i>The Routledge Companion to Britain in the Twentieth Century</i> (2009) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/0415275350/">excerpt and text search</a></li>\n<li>Loades, David, ed. <i>Reader\'s Guide to British History</i> (2 vol 2003), 1610pp</li>\n<li>Rasor, Eugene L. <i>Winston S. Churchill, 1874\xe2\x80\x931965: A Comprehensive Historiography and Annotated Bibliography</i> (2000) 712pp <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.questia.com/library/71893609/winston-s-churchill-1874-1965-a-comprehensive-historiography">online at Questia</a>; also <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/winstonschurchil00raso">online free</a></li>\n<li>Schlatter, Richard, ed. <i>Recent Views on British History: Essays on Historical Writing Since 1966</i> (1984)</li>\n<li>Williams, Chris, ed. <i>A Companion to Nineteenth-Century Britain</i> (Blackwell, 2006); 33 essays by experts; 624pp <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/B000W7ZSO4/">excerpt and text search</a></li>\n<li>Wrigley, Chris, ed. <i>A Companion to Early Twentieth-Century Britain</i> (Blackwell Companions to British History) (2009) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/1405189991/">excerpt and text search</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_sources">Primary sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Primary sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r853264625"/><div class="refbegin" style="">\n<div style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
